Third Objection: Major Sins Negate Faith
Opponents argue major sins negate faith; author begins response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opponents' argument that major sins contradict faith and the author's initial rebuttal.

Core Idea
Major sins do not automatically remove faith; pity in punishment is not mercy.

This lesson examines a key objection raised against the Sunni position that major sins do not negate faith. The opponents use Quranic verses to argue that the Prophet is merciful only to believers, and since he is commanded not to pity fornicators, they must be unbelievers. The author begins his response by denying the premise and clarifying the intended meaning of the verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the passage where the opponents state their claim: committing a major sin negates faith. Then read the translation.
Notice the strong language: 'yunafi al-iman'.
2
Identify the evidence
Find the two sets of Quranic verses used: one showing the Prophet's mercy to believers, the other commanding no pity for fornicators. Understand how they are combined.
3
Understand the logic
Trace the logical chain: mercy is for believers; Prophet is commanded not to have pity (ra'fa) on fornicators; therefore fornicators are not believers.
Note that 'ra'fa' is a form of mercy.
4
Examine the response
Read the author's initial reply: he does not concede the premise and begins to explain the verse's meaning. Notice that the response is incomplete in this passage.
5
Reflect on the dispute
Consider why this objection is important for the doctrine of faith and sin. The author's full answer would continue beyond this excerpt.

They said: Committing a major sin is contrary to faith, because He, exalted, established for the Messenger (s) the attribute of mercy towards the believers, saying: 'And He is to the believers merciful' [al-Ahzab 33:43], and said: 'To the believers kind and merciful' [al-Tawba 9:128]. And the answer to this: we do not concede that committing a major sin is contrary to faith. The meaning of the verse: 'Do not let...'

Commentary
This passage is the third objection and the beginning of the author's response. The opponents argue that committing a major sin (kabira) contradicts faith. They present a proof from two sets of verses: one shows that the Prophet (s) is characterized as merciful and kind to the believers; the other (al-Nur 24:2) commands the Prophet not to have pity on fornicators when executing the penalty. Since pity is a trait of mercy reserved for believers, and the Prophet is told not to pity fornicators, this implies fornicators are not believers. Thus the act of fornication negates faith. The author begins his answer by denying the premise: he does not concede that a major sin contradicts faith. He starts to explain the meaning of the verse (likely 'do not let pity seize you' means do not prevent the punishment out of pity, not that the person is a non-believer). However, the answer is incomplete in the available text, breaking off mid-sentence. The author intended to further clarify that the verse does not indicate the fornicator is an unbeliever.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that because the Quran commands not to pity fornicators, it means fornicators are not believers.
Correction: The author clarifies that the prohibition of pity is about not preventing the punishment out of mercy, not about declaring the person an unbeliever.

Two Refutations of Fisq Contradicting Iman
Two answers refuting that fisq contradicts iman via Quran 49:7.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two distinct responses to the objection that fisq (immorality) cannot coexist with iman based on Quran 49:7.

Core Idea
Contrast in language does not imply logical contradiction.

The objectors claim that Quran 49:7 shows fisq is contradictory to iman, implying actions are part of iman. Our author provides two powerful refutations: first, that the verse only shows a contrast of preference, not logical opposition; second, even if it did show opposition, other verses prove that sin does not negate iman. Let's examine these arguments closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the verse
First, understand the opponents' claim: they cite Quran 49:7 to argue that fisq contradicts iman, so iman must include actions that prevent fisq.
The verse lists kufr, fisq, and disobedience together as hated things.
2
Study the first answer
The first answer denies that the verse implies logical contradiction. The author uses an analogy: 'I love knowledge and hate fisq' does not make fisq the opposite of knowledge. Similarly, the verse only shows love for iman and dislike for fisq.
The phrase 'خرط القتاد' (cutting a thorny tree) indicates the argument is far-fetched.
3
Study the second answer
The second answer concedes the verse implies contradiction but argues that does not prove actions are part of iman. Quran 6:82 shows believers can commit injustice (sin) without losing iman.
This answer uses another verse to counter the objection.
4
Address the counter-objection
A hypothetical objector says: if the verse doesn't show contradiction with fisq, then it also doesn't show contradiction with kufr. The author agrees, but notes that kufr's contradiction is proven by other evidence.
This shows the verse is neutral on the issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: مما يدل على أن الأعمال داخلة في حقيقة الإيمان أنه جعل الفسوق مناقضا للإيمان لا يجامعه ، وذلك قوله سبحانه: ﴿وَلَكِنَّ اللهَ حَبَّبَ إِلَيْكُمُ الْإِيمَنَ وَزَيَّنَهُ فِي قُلُوبِكُمْ وَكَرَّة إلَيْكُمُ الْكُفْرَ وَالْفُسُوقَ وَالْعِصْيَانَ ﴾ [الحجرات: ۷] . ولو كان الإيمان هو التصديق وحده لجامع الفسوق والعصيان . ويجاب عن ذلك بأحد جوابين: الأول: لا تُسلم أنَّ هذه الآية دالة على أنّ الفسوق مناقض للإيمان لا يجامعه ، أفترى أني لو قلتُ : (إني أحب العلم وأكره الفسوق)، دلَّ هذا على أنَّ الفسوق نقيض العلم، وأنه لا يجامعه ؟ فإن دل هذا الكلام على مناقضة الفسوق للعلم دلت الآية الكريمة على مناقضة الفسوق للإيمان، ودون ذلك خرط القتاد . والثاني: سلَّمنا أنَّ الآية تدل على مناقضة الفسوق للإيمان ، لكن ذلك لا يدل على أن الإيمان هو ما ذكرتم من التصديق وعمل الطاعات عند كل أحد ، وذلك لأن ما دلت عليه هذه الآية بزعمكم قد عارضه ما يدل على ما ذهبنا من مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَلَمْ يَلْبِسُوا إِيمَانَهُم بِظُلْمٍ﴾ [الأنعام: ۸۲] . فإن قلت: فإذا كانت الآية لا تدل على أن الفسوق مناقض للإيمان، فإنها لا تدل أيضا على أنَّ الكفر مناقض للإيمان. فالجواب أن نسلم أن الآية لا تدل على هذا ولا ذاك ، وكون الكفر مناقضا للإيمان ثابت بغير هذا الدليل.
They said: Among what indicates that actions are included in the reality of iman is that He made fisq (immorality) contradictory to iman, not coexisting with it, and that is His saying, Exalted is He: {But Allah has endeared to you the faith and adorned it in your hearts and has made hateful to you disbelief, fisq, and disobedience} [Al-Hujurat 49:7]. And if iman were mere tasdiq (assent), fisq and disobedience would coexist with it. And it is answered with one of two answers: The first: We do not accept that this verse indicates that fisq is contradictory to iman, not coexisting with it. Do you not see that if I say 'I love knowledge and hate fisq', does that indicate that fisq is the opposite of knowledge and does not coexist with it? For if this speech indicates the contradiction of fisq to knowledge, then the noble verse would indicate the contradiction of fisq to iman—and that is far-fetched. The second: We accept that the verse indicates the contradiction of fisq to iman, but that does not indicate that iman is what you mentioned of tasdiq and performing acts of obedience in the view of everyone, because what this verse indicates, in your claim, is opposed by what indicates our view, such as His saying, Exalted is He: {Those who believed and did not mix their iman with injustice} [Al-An'am 6:82]. If you say: So if the verse does not indicate that fisq contradicts iman, then it also does not indicate that kufr contradicts iman. The answer: We accept that the verse does not indicate either, and the fact that kufr contradicts iman is established by other evidence.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a kalam refutation of the claim that actions are part of the reality of iman. The objectors cite Quran 49:7, where Allah says He has made iman beloved and kufr, fisq, and disobedience hateful. They argue that if fisq is made hateful, it must be contradictory to iman, implying that iman is not mere assent but includes actions that oppose fisq. The author gives two distinct answers. First answer: The verse does not necessarily imply a conceptual contradiction; it only shows a contrast of preference, not opposition. The author illustrates with a parallel statement 'I love knowledge and hate fisq'—this does not make fisq the opposite of knowledge, but merely a disliked thing. Similarly, the verse shows love for iman and dislike for fisq, not that fisq is the opposite of iman. He calls this argument far-fetched ('خرط القتاد', literally 'the cutting of the [thorny] tree'). Second answer: Even if we accept that the verse shows a contradiction, that does not prove that iman is tasdiq plus actions, because other verses, like 6:82, show that believers can have iman while committing injustice (sin), which suggests that sin does not negate iman. He then addresses a counter-objection: If the verse does not show contradiction with fisq, then it also doesn't show contradiction with kufr? He answers that indeed it does not, but the contradiction of kufr with iman is established by other, stronger evidence. Thus, the verse is neutral on the issue.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الفسوق
التصديق
مناقضة
آية الحجرات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any verse that contrasts iman with fisq proves that fisq logically cannot coexist with iman, implying iman includes actions.
Correction: Contrast in language (e.g., love vs. hate) does not imply logical contradiction; it may only express a difference in preference. Other verses show that believers can commit sins without losing iman.

Checkpoint
In the first answer to the objection from Quran 49:7, what analogy does the author use to show that the verse does not imply a logical contradiction?
A) The analogy of loving knowledge and hating fisq
B) The analogy of mixing iman with injustice
C) The analogy of cutting a thorny tree
D) The analogy of the Prophet's mercy

Key Takeaway
The objection from Quran 49:7 fails because verbal contrast does not entail logical contradiction, and other verses confirm that sin does not negate iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever feel that your iman has completely vanished? How does the second argument (using 6:82) challenge that feeling? What does it demand from you now?
?
The author uses an analogy: 'I love knowledge and hate fisq.' In your own life, do you genuinely love iman and hate sin? If not, what is holding you back from that love? What concrete step will you take today to strengthen that love?
?
The author emphasizes that kufr's contradiction with iman is established by other evidence, not by this verse. Are you clear on what separates kufr from fisq in your own heart? Could you be confusing major sins with disbelief, thus losing hope or falling into false security? What will you do to gain clarity?

Major Sin Does Not Negate Iman: Refuting the Quran 24:2 Objection
Answer to the objection that the Prophet's command not to be merciful to adulterers proves they are not believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that major sin negates iman based on Quran 24:2 is answered by distinguishing between mercy in punishment and mercy in faith.

Core Idea
Major sin does not negate iman; the command against mercy is about enforcing punishment, not about faith.

This lesson addresses a common objection from those who argue that committing a major sin, like adultery, removes a person from faith. They cite verses where Allah describes the Prophet as merciful to believers, but commands not to show pity to adulterers in the punishment verse. We will see how the answer clarifies that the prohibition is about executing the legal penalty, not about the sinner's belief.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection carefully: it uses two verses showing the Prophet's mercy to believers, and one verse prohibiting mercy to adulterers, concluding that adulterers are not believers.
Notice how the objection constructs a logical contradiction.
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Identify the three Quranic verses cited: Al-Ahzab 33:43, At-Tawbah 9:128 (mercy to believers), and An-Nur 24:2 (no mercy to adulterers). Think about their contexts.
The objection assumes mercy in one context equals mercy in another.
3
Grasp the counter-interpretation
The answer rejects the premise that major sin contradicts iman, and reinterprets Quran 24:2 as prohibiting leniency in executing prescribed punishments, not as a statement about the adulterer's faith.
The key distinction is between mercy in punishment and mercy in belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: فعل الكبيرة ينافي الإيمان ؛ لأنه سبحانه أثبت للرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم صفة الرحمة بالمؤمنين فقال: وَكَانَ بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَحِيمًا ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٣] وقال: ﴿بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَءُوفٌ رَّحِيمٌ ) [ التوبة : ۱۲۸ ] ، وقد أمره سبحانه ألَّا يَرْأَفَ بِالزُّنَاةِ فقال: وَلَا تَأْخُذَكُر بِهِمَا رَأْفَةٌ فِي دِينِ اللهِ) [النور: ٢] فدل ذلك على أنَّ الزاني ليس بمؤمن، وليس لعدم إيمانه سبب إلا ارتكاب هذه الكبيرة. والجواب عن هذا: أنا لا نسلم أنَّ فعل الكبيرة منافٍ للإيمان، ومعنى الآية: لا تَحْمِلَنَّكُمُ الشَّفَقَةُ بهم على أن تُسْقِطُوا حدود الله تعالى بعد وجوبها.
They said: The commission of a major sin contradicts iman, because He, Exalted, established for the Messenger, peace be upon him, the attribute of mercy towards the believers, saying: {And He (Allah) is with the believers Merciful} [Al-Ahzab 33:43], and said: {To the believers (he is) kind and merciful} [At-Tawbah 9:128], and He, Exalted, commanded him not to have mercy on adulterers, saying: {And let not pity for them restrain you in the religion of Allah} [An-Nur 24:2]. So that indicates that the adulterer is not a believer, and there is no reason for his lack of iman except committing this major sin. The answer to this: We do not accept that the commission of a major sin contradicts iman, and the meaning of the verse is: Let not compassion for them cause you to abandon the prescribed punishments of Allah after they become obligatory.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer regarding the relationship between major sins and iman. The objectors argue that since Allah describes the Prophet as merciful to believers (Quran 33:43, 9:128), but commands him not to be merciful to adulterers (Quran 24:2), it follows that adulterers are not believers, implying that iman excludes those who commit major sins. The author answers by rejecting the premise that major sin contradicts iman. Instead, he interprets the verse about not showing pity in the context of executing legal punishments (hudud): the prohibition is against allowing compassion to prevent the enforcement of Allah's prescribed penalties after they are due. Thus, the verse does not negate the adulterer's iman, only the permissibility of leniency in punishment.

Key Terms
الكبيرة (major sin)
الرأفة (mercy/pity)
حدود الله (prescribed punishments)
الزنا (adultery)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The command to not show pity to adulterers in Quran 24:2 means that adulterers are not believers; therefore, major sin negates iman.
Correction: The verse is about executing legal punishments, not about the faith status of the sinner. Major sin does not remove iman.

Checkpoint

A) Do not show mercy to adulterers at all
B) Do not be compassionate to them before the punishment
C) Do not let compassion cause you to abandon the prescribed punishment after it is due
D) Do not treat adulterers as believers

Key Takeaway
The command to not show pity to adulterers is about enforcing Allah's prescribed punishments, not a statement that they are outside the fold of faith.

The objectors used the Prophet's mercy as a proof that adulterers are not believers. Refuting the Disgrace Objection: This World vs. the Hereafter
Answer to the objection based on Quran 66:8 and 5:33

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author resolves the apparent contradiction between the promise not to disgrace believers on the Day of Resurrection and the worldly punishment of brigands.

Core Idea
Worldly disgrace does not negate iman; only disgrace on the Day of Resurrection does.

This lesson addresses a key objection raised against the view that actions are part of iman. Opponents cite two Quranic verses that seem to conflict: one promises believers they will not be disgraced on the Last Day, while another mentions that brigands face disgrace in this world. The author shows that the verses refer to different times—this world and the Hereafter—and thus there is no contradiction. By understanding this distinction, you will see why worldly punishment does not imply loss of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the argument's flow.
Pay attention to the Quranic quotes.
2
Identify the two verses and their temporal references
Notice that the first verse (66:8) mentions 'Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and believers' explicitly referring to the Day of Resurrection. The second verse (5:33) states 'disgrace in this world and punishment in the Hereafter' for brigands.
The key is the temporal difference.
3
Understand the logical point: no implication of incompatibility across times
The author argues that the promise about the Hereafter does not preclude worldly disgrace. The two are separate domains.
This refutes the objection that disgrace in this world would contradict the promise.
4
Reflect on the significance for the actions-iman debate
If worldly disgrace could affect iman, then the objection would stand. But since it doesn't, the objection is neutralized.
This lesson helps clarify that outward punishment does not necessarily indicate loss of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: إن الله تعالى لا يخزي المؤمنين ؛ بدليل قوله جلت كلمته: ﴿يَوْمَ لَا يُخْزِي اللَّهُ النَّبِيَّ وَالَّذِينَ ءَامَنُواْ مَعَهُ ﴾ [التحريم: ۸] والله يخزي قطاع الطريق، بدليل قوله سبحانه في شأنهم: ﴿ذَلِكَ لَهُمْ خِزْيٌ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَلَهُمْ فِي الْآخِرَةِ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمٌ﴾ [المائدة: ٣٣] . ذلك: أنه ليس في الآيتين دلالة على ما زعموا من قريب أو بعيد ؛ فإن الآية الأولى دلت على نفي أن يخزي الله تعالى الرسول ومَن آمن به عامة في يوم القيامة ، والآية الثانية أثبتت الخزي لهؤلاء العصاة في الدُّنيا، وإذا دلَّت الآية الأولى على منافاة الخزي في يوم القيامة للإيمان، فإنّها لا تدلّ على منافاة الخزي في الدنيا للإيمان، ولا يلزم من منافاة الخزي في الآخرة للإيمان منافاة الخزي في الدُّنيا له.
They said: Allah, Exalted, does not disgrace the believers, as evidenced by His words, Majestic is His speech: {On the Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him} [At-Tahrim 66:8]. And Allah disgraces brigands, as evidenced by His words, Exalted, concerning them: {That is for them a disgrace in this world, and for them in the Hereafter a great punishment} [Al-Ma'idah 5:33]. The answer: There is in the two verses no indication of what they claim, near or far. For the first verse indicates the negation that Allah will disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him generally on the Day of Resurrection, and the second verse affirms disgrace for these sinners in this world. And if the first verse indicates the incompatibility of disgrace on the Day of Resurrection with iman, it does not indicate the incompatibility of disgrace in this world with iman, and the incompatibility of disgrace in the Hereafter with iman does not necessitate the incompatibility of disgrace in this world with it.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage refutes the objection that actions are part of iman because Allah promises not to disgrace believers (Quran 66:8) but disgraces bandits in this world (Quran 5:33). The objectors infer that those who are disgraced in this world cannot be believers. The author responds by pointing out a temporal distinction: the first verse specifically refers to the Day of Resurrection, promising that believers will not be disgraced on that day. The second verse describes disgrace in this world for bandits, which does not negate their potential iman. There is no logical necessity that disgrace in this world entails disgrace in the Hereafter, nor that disgrace in the Hereafter is incompatible with temporary worldly disgrace. Thus, the objection fails.

Key Terms
الخزي (disgrace)
قطاع الطريق (brigands/bandits)
يوم القيامة (Day of Resurrection)
الدنيا (this world)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a believer is disgraced in this world (e.g., punished for a crime), that means they have lost their iman.
Correction: The Quranic promise of no disgrace applies specifically to the Day of Resurrection, not to this world. Worldly punishment does not negate iman.

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between the two verses cited in this argument?
A) One refers to believers, the other to disbelievers
B) One refers to disgrace in the Hereafter, the other to disgrace in this world
C) One is about the Prophet, the other about common people
D) One is in the Quran, the other is a hadith

Key Takeaway
Disgrace in this world does not contradict the promise of no disgrace on the Day of Resurrection, and therefore does not negate iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a Muslim facing public disgrace—whether for a crime or for being tested—do you secretly question the strength of their iman? How can you train your heart to separate worldly consequences from ultimate spiritual standing, as this lesson demands?
?
If you were the one disgraced in this world for a sin, would you despair of your iman? Reflect: does your hope in Allah's promise of no disgrace on the Day of Resurrection outweigh your fear of worldly shame? What concrete step can you take today to strengthen that hope?
?
How often do you judge others' faith based on their worldly circumstances? Starting today, will you commit to withholding judgment about anyone's iman because of trials or punishments they face in this life, knowing that only the Hereafter reveals true standing?

Why Omitting Hajj Does Not Necessarily Negate Iman
Objection-and-answer regarding Hajj omission and disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that omitting Hajj makes one a disbeliever, using two interpretations of Quran 3:97.

Core Idea
Omitting an act is not disbelief; only denial of its obligation is.

Some argue that a capable person who fails to perform Hajj without excuse is a disbeliever, citing Quran 3:97. This lesson examines the objection and the author's two-part response, which clarifies that the verse refers to denial of the rite, not mere neglect.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Objection
Read the objection carefully: the claim is that leaving Hajj without excuse equals disbelief, supported by Quran 3:97.
Note the assumption that action is part of iman.
2
Identify the First Answer
The author first rejects the premise that omitting Hajj makes one a disbeliever, and says the Quranic phrase is an independent statement.
3
Identify the Second Answer
The author offers an alternative interpretation: 'kafara' means denial of Hajj rites, which cannot apply to one who affirms them.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.
4
Reflect on the Distinction
Consider the difference between omitting an obligation and denying its validity. This distinction is key to understanding the author's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: إذا ترك المستطيعُ الحج من غير عذر فهو كافر مع أنه مصدق ؛ بدليل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا وَمَن كَفَرَ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ غَنِيٌّ عَنِ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾ [آل عمران: ۹۷] فلو لم يكن العمل جزءاً من حقيقة الإيمان لما صح ذلك. ويجاب عن هذا بأنا لا نسلم كفرَ من ترك الحج من غير عذر ، وقوله تعالى: (ومن كفر) الآية ، كلام مُستأنف ، أو نقول: معنى (كفر) جَحَدَ مناسك الحج ولم يصدق بها، وذلك لا يتصور مع التصديق المفروض فيمن ذكرتم.
They said: If a capable person leaves Hajj without excuse, he is a disbeliever while he is a musaddiq (one who assents), as evidenced by His saying, Exalted is He: {And due to Allah from the people is Hajj to the House, for whoever is able to find a way thereto. And whoever disbelieves, then indeed Allah is free from need of the worlds} [Aal-Imran 3:97]. For if action were not a part of the reality of iman, that would not be correct. It is answered by: We do not accept that one who leaves Hajj without excuse is a disbeliever, and His saying, Exalted is He: 'And whoever disbelieves' is an independent statement, or we say: The meaning of 'disbelieves' is denies the rites of Hajj and does not believe in them, and that is inconceivable with the assumed tasdiq in the person you mentioned.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection that a capable person who fails to perform Hajj without excuse is a disbeliever (kafir), which would imply that iman includes performing Hajj. The author rejects the premise. He offers two interpretations: (1) The phrase 'and whoever disbelieves' in Quran 3:97 is an independent statement (musta'naf), not directly linking to the preceding command about Hajj. (2) The word 'disbelieves' here means to deny or reject the obligation of Hajj itself, not merely to omit it while accepting its obligation. Since the objector presupposes that the person is a musaddiq (assents), such denial is impossible. Therefore, the verse does not support the claim that omitting Hajj renders a believer a disbeliever.

Key Terms
الحج (Hajj)
المستطيع (the capable one)
الكفر (disbelief)
جحد (denial)
مناسك الحج (rites of Hajj)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that failing to perform an obligatory act like Hajj automatically makes one a disbeliever.
Correction: The author shows that disbelief (kufr) here means denial of the obligation, not just neglect.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what does the word 'kafara' (disbelieves) in Quran 3:97 mean?
A) Leaves Hajj without excuse
B) Denies the rites of Hajj
C) Does not complete the rituals properly
D) Travels without performing Hajj

Key Takeaway
The Quranic threat of disbelief for neglecting Hajj applies only to those who deny its obligation, not to those who omit it while affirming its duty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there any obligations of Allah that you have neglected while still affirming their importance? How does this passage challenge you to examine the difference between your belief and your actions?
?
When you fail to perform an obligatory act, do you ever rationalize it by saying 'I still believe'? How does the author's distinction between omission and denial expose a potential hypocrisy in your heart?
?
The Quran threatens with disbelief those who deny the rites of Hajj. What rites or commands of Allah have you allowed yourself to be complacent about? What would it mean for you to truly affirm them not just with your tongue but with your actions?

Refuting the claim that not judging by Allah's revelation negates iman (Quran 5:44)
Answer to the objection that those who do not judge by Allah's revelation are disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the apparent contradiction in Quran 5:44 is resolved by clarifying that the verse refers to denial or contempt for divine law, not to every instance of misjudgment.

Core Idea
Not every failure to judge by revelation is disbelief; only denial or contempt counts.

This lesson addresses a powerful objection: If iman is only tasdiq, why does Quran 5:44 label those who do not judge by Allah's revelation as disbelievers? The author shows that the verse is misapplied when taken literally. He offers a two-fold interpretation that protects the definition of iman as tasdiq alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the passage's opening lines where the objectors present their argument: how can someone who has tasdiq be called a disbeliever?
Notice the use of Quran 5:44 as evidence.
2
Identify the two parts of the answer
The author gives two interpretations of 'whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed'. Find both and understand each one.
The first interpretation equates 'not judging' with 'not believing'; the second adds contempt for divine law.
3
Understand the reasoning
Both interpretations preserve the principle that disbelief stems from a lack of tasdiq or rejection of authority, not from mere error in judgment.
This refutes the objection.
4
Reflect on the broader significance
Consider how this answer protects the core definition of iman as tasdiq, while acknowledging the gravity of rejecting Allah's law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: التصديق موجود فيمن لم يحكم بما أنزل الله ، والله قد حكم عليه بالكفر في قوله سبحانه: ﴿وَمَن لَّمْ يَحْكُم بِمَا أَنزَلَ اللَّهُ فَأُولَيكَ هُمُ الكَفِرُونَ ﴾ [المائدة: ٤٤] ، فدل ذلك على أن الإيمان هو التصديق والعمل. ويجاب عن هذا بمثل ما أجبنا به عن الآية السابقة من الوجهين، وحاصله : أنَّ معنى: (من لم يحكم بما أنزل الله من لم يصدق ، أو من لم يحكم بشيء مما أنزل الله معتقدا أنه لا يصلح للحكم، أو نحو ذلك.
They said: Tasdiq exists in one who does not judge by what Allah has revealed, and Allah has ruled him as a disbeliever in His saying: {And whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed, then it is those who are the disbelievers} [Al-Ma'idah 5:44]. So that indicates that iman is tasdiq and action. It is answered with the same two aspects with which we answered the previous verse. The summary is: The meaning of 'whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed' is whoever does not believe, or whoever does not judge by anything that Allah has revealed while believing that it is not suitable for judgment, or the like.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents another objection: The Quran (5:44) labels those who do not judge by Allah's revelation as disbelievers, yet they have tasdiq (assent). The objectors argue that this proves iman includes action (judging by revelation), because otherwise the label 'disbeliever' would be inappropriate. The author gives the same type of answer as for the previous Hajj verse. He says the phrase 'whoever does not judge' can be interpreted in two ways: either it means 'whoever does not believe (in the revelation)', i.e., outright denial, or it means 'whoever refuses to judge by any part of revelation while believing it is not suitable for judgment'—which implies a rejection of divine authority, thus disbelief. In both cases, the verse applies to someone who lacks genuine tasdiq, not to a believer who errs in judgment. Thus, the objection fails.

Key Terms
الحكم بما أنزل الله
التصديق
الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Every instance of not judging by Allah's revelation constitutes disbelief, even if the person has tasdiq.
Correction: The verse is restricted to those who deny revelation or reject its authority, not to believers who err in judgment.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what is one possible meaning of 'whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed'?
A) Anyone who makes a mistake in legal ruling
B) Whoever does not believe in the revelation
C) Whoever follows a different school of thought
D) Whoever is not a scholar of fiqh

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse about judging by revelation does not undermine the definition of iman as tasdiq; it applies only to those who deny or reject divine law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever knowingly preferred a worldly system or your own desires over a clear Islamic ruling in your decisions? What does that reveal about the state of your iman? Will you sincerely repent and commit to submitting fully to Allah's judgment, even when it is difficult?
?
The verse warns of disbelief for those who reject divine law. Do you truly fear that label, or have you become complacent with selective obedience? In which areas of your life do you find yourself most resistant to judging by what Allah has revealed?
?
When you encounter a part of Islamic law that conflicts with modern norms or personal convenience, how do you react internally? Are you tempted to dismiss it or rationalize it away? This lesson teaches that contempt for revelation is a form of kufr. Examine your heart: Is there any contempt hidden within you?

Refuting the Hadith Objection: Fornication and Iman
Answer to the hadith that a fornicator is not a believer while fornicating.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith 'the fornicator does not fornicate while a believer' is reconciled with the Sunni position that major sins do not negate iman.

Core Idea
Sins negate iman only when considered lawful, not when committed out of weakness.

A powerful hadith seems to say that a fornicator cannot be a believer, which would support those who say iman includes action and is lost by sin. But the scholars of Ahl al-Sunna offer clear interpretations that preserve the distinction between sinning while acknowledging the prohibition and outright rejection of the law. This lesson presents the two main answers given in the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and hadith
First, read the objection presented: the hadith is used to argue that fornicators are disbelievers because iman includes action.
The hadith is authentic but its interpretation is key.
2
Understand the first answer
The first answer limits the hadith to those who commit the sin while considering it lawful (mustahill). This is kufr because it rejects Allah's prohibition.
3
Understand the second answer
The second answer reinterprets 'believer' (mu'min) in the hadith as 'one secure from punishment,' so the sin temporarily removes that security, not iman itself.
This is a linguistic interpretation.
4
Connect to the broader doctrine
Reflect on how these answers protect the Sunni position: iman is belief and affirmation, and major sins do not remove it unless accompanied by istihlal.
This is a key theological principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: الزاني وشارب الخمر ونحوهما كفار ؛ بدليل قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «لا يزني الزاني وهو مؤمن، ولا يشرب الخمر حين يشربها وهو مؤمن وذلك دليل على أن الإيمان يتضمن العمل. ويجاب عن ذلك بأنَّ المراد: هو الذي يزني وهو مُستحل لِزِنَاهُ، والذي يشرب الخمر مستحلا لشربها ، أو المراد بمؤمن في قوله : وهو مؤمن آمِنْ مِن عذاب الله تعالى
They said: The fornicator and the wine drinker and the like are disbelievers, as evidenced by his saying, peace be upon him: 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer, nor does the wine drinker drink while he is a believer.' And that is evidence that iman includes action. It is answered with: The intended meaning is the one who fornicates while considering it lawful, and who drinks wine while considering it lawful, or the intended meaning of 'believer' in his saying 'while he is a believer' is one who is secure from the punishment of Allah, Exalted.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith-based objection: The Prophet said that a fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer, implying that iman is negated by the act. The objectors take this as proof that iman includes action. The author provides two answers. First, the hadith refers to a person who commits the sin while considering it lawful (mustahill) – such a person rejects the divine prohibition, which indeed negates iman. This is different from a believer who commits the sin while knowing it is wrong but does not consider it lawful. Second, the word 'believer' (mu'min) in the hadith may mean 'one who is secure from Allah's punishment' (amin min adhab Allah), i.e., committing the sin nullifies that security temporarily, not that the person loses iman entirely. The answer is incomplete in the provided pages, but the given portion clarifies the main refutations.

Key Terms
الزاني (fornicator)
شارب الخمر (wine drinker)
مستحل (considering lawful)
آمن من عذاب الله (secure from Allah's punishment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith proves that any major sin like fornication or drinking wine removes iman completely, making the person a disbeliever.
Correction: The hadith only applies to those who consider the sin lawful (istihlal), which is kufr. For a believer who sins while acknowledging its prohibition, iman remains, though the sin is still major.

Checkpoint
According to one of the author's answers, what does the word 'mu'min' (believer) in the hadith mean?
A) One who has faith in Allah
B) One who is secure from punishment
C) One who performs all obligations
D) One who never sins

Key Takeaway
The hadith about the fornicator does not prove that major sins destroy iman; it either applies to those who consider sin lawful or refers to temporary loss of security from punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking 'it's not that bad' or 'Allah will forgive me anyway'? How close is that to the mindset of istihlal, and what can you do to guard your heart against it?
?
The second answer reminds you that during sin, you are not secure from Allah's punishment. How does that realization strike you? The next time you are tempted, will you remember that your sense of security might be false?
?
This lesson shows that even a clear hadith can have deeper meanings. When you read a verse or hadith that seems harsh, do you trust that scholars have sound explanations, or do you allow despair to creep in? How can you strengthen your reliance on sound scholarship?

Faith and Worldly Disgrace
Responds to argument that iman prevents worldly disgrace using Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational distinction between disgrace in this world and disgrace in the Hereafter, and why faith does not guarantee immunity from worldly disgrace.

Core Idea
Faith saves from disgrace in the Hereafter, not necessarily from disgrace in this world.

This lesson addresses a common assumption: that true believers are never disgraced in this world. The objectors cite Quranic verses to argue that Allah does not disgrace believers. Through a careful analysis of the verses, the author shows that the verses only refer to disgrace on the Day of Judgment, not in this life. Thus, faith and worldly disgrace are not incompatible.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the two verses cited
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the two Quranic verses used by the objectors: 66:8 and 5:33. Observe how they are presented as evidence.
Notice the objectors' assumption that iman prevents all forms of disgrace.
2
Analyze the response's logical distinction
The response points out that the first verse speaks about the Day of Resurrection, while the second speaks about disgrace in this world. Understand how the author shows that the verses do not support the claim.
The key is the difference between dunya and akhirah.
3
Contrast the two types of disgrace
Reflect on the difference between disgrace in this world and disgrace in the Hereafter. Why does the incompatibility of faith with one not imply incompatibility with the other?
This highlights the necessity of precise scriptural interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان حقيقة الإيمان قالوا: إن الله تعالى لا يخزي المؤمنين ; بدليل قوله جلت كلمته: ﴿يَوْمَ لَا يُخْزِي اللَّهُ النَّبِيَّ وَالَّذِينَ ءَامَنُواْ مَعَهُ ﴾ [التحريم: ۸] والله يخزي قطاع الطريق، بدليل قوله سبحانه في شأنهم: ﴿ذَلِكَ لَهُمْ خِزْيٌ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَلَهُمْ فِي الْآخِرَةِ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمٌ﴾ [المائدة: ٣٣] . ذلك : أنه ليس في الآيتين دلالة على ما زعموا من قريب أو بعيد ; فإن الآية الأولى دلت على نفي أن يخزي الله تعالى الرسول ومَن آمن به عامة في يوم القيامة ، والآية الثانية أثبتت الخزي لهؤلاء العصاة في الدُّنيا، وإذا دلَّت الآية الأولى على منافاة الخزي في يوم القيامة للإيمان، فإنّها لا تدلّ على منافاة الخزي في الدنيا للإيمان، ولا يلزم من منافاة الخزي في الآخرة للإيمان منافاة الخزي في الدُّنيا له.
Statement of the reality of faith. They said: Indeed, Allah does not disgrace the believers, as evidence of His words: 'On the Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him' [Quran 66:8], and Allah disgraces highway robbers, as evidence of His words: 'That is for them a disgrace in this world, and for them in the Hereafter is a great punishment' [Quran 5:33]. That: there is no indication in the two verses of what they claim, near or far; for the first verse indicates the negation that Allah disgraces the Messenger and those who believe with him generally on the Day of Resurrection, and the second verse established disgrace for these sinners in this world. If the first verse indicates the incompatibility of disgrace on the Day of Resurrection with faith, it does not indicate the incompatibility of disgrace in this world with faith, and the incompatibility of disgrace in the Hereafter with faith does not necessitate the incompatibility of disgrace in this world with it.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from those who argue that iman (faith) prevents disgrace, citing Quran 66:8 which states that Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and believers on the Day of Judgment, and Quran 5:33 which mentions disgrace for highway robbers. The response clarifies that the first verse only negates disgrace in the Hereafter, not in this world, while the second verse establishes disgrace in this world for sinners. Therefore, there is no contradiction; a believer can be disgraced in this world while being saved from disgrace in the Hereafter. So the claim that iman prevents all disgrace is refuted.

Key Terms
خزي (khiziy/disgrace)
الإيمان (iman)
يوم القيامة (yawm al-qiyamah)
الدُّنيا (dunya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that true believers are never disgraced in this world.
Correction: The Quranic verses only guarantee that believers will not be disgraced on the Day of Resurrection, not in this life. Worldly disgrace is not contradictory to faith.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the response to the first objection?
A) That believers are never disgraced
B) That disgrace in the Hereafter is incompatible with faith, but disgrace in this world is not
C) That all sinners are disbelievers
D) That the verses contradict each other

Key Takeaway
Faith ensures safety from disgrace on the Day of Judgment, but it does not prevent disgrace in this world.

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate

Refutation of Claim that Leaving Hajj Constitutes Kufr
Refutes argument that not performing Hajj with ability is kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why leaving Hajj without excuse does not constitute disbelief, and how the Quranic verse (3:97) is interpreted to preserve the principle that faith is affirmation, not action.

Core Idea
Not performing Hajj is not kufr; only denying its obligation is.

Some have argued that failing to perform Hajj when able is an act of disbelief, citing Quran 3:97. The classical response clarifies that the verse refers to denial of the obligation, not mere non-performance. This lesson examines that refutation and its implications for the relationship between faith and actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note how the objection is phrased and how the response begins with 'we do not accept'.
The passage is short; read it slowly to grasp the argument flow.
2
Identify the objection and its proof
Find the claim of the objectors: that abandoning Hajj without excuse is kufr. Note their proof: Quran 3:97 uses the term 'kafir' for such a person.
The objectors assume that since the verse calls that person a 'kafir', action must be part of faith.
3
Analyze the response's two arguments
The response offers two interpretations: (1) The verse is an independent statement (musta'naf), not connected to the previous clause. (2) 'Kufr' here means denial (juhud) of the obligation, not mere abandonment.
Both interpretations preserve that the person's faith (tasdiq) remains intact.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this distinction matters: it shows that kufr is about belief, not action. Actions can be sinful but not disbelief unless they involve denial of a known obligation.
This aligns with the Ash'ari view that faith is affirmation (tasdiq), not actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: إذا ترك المستطيعُ الحج من غير عذر فهو كافر مع أنه مصدق ; بدليل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا وَمَن كَفَرَ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ غَنِيٌّ عَنِ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾ [آل عمران: ۹۷] فلو لم يكن العمل جزءاً من حقيقة الإيمان لما صح ذلك. ويجاب عن هذا بأنا لا نسلم كفرَ من ترك الحج من غير عذر ، وقوله تعالى: (ومن كفر) الآية ، كلام مُستأنف ، أو نقول: معنى (كفر) جَحَدَ مناسك الحج ولم يصدق بها، وذلك لا يتصور مع التصديق المفروض فيمن ذكرتم.
They said: If the capable one abandons Hajj without excuse, he is a disbeliever despite being a believer, as evidence of His words: 'And to Allah is the pilgrimage to the House, for whoever is able to find a way to it. And whoever disbelieves, then indeed Allah is free from need of the worlds' [Quran 3:97]. So if action were not part of the reality of faith, that would not be valid. And the response to this is that we do not accept the disbelief of one who abandons Hajj without excuse, and His words 'and whoever disbelieves' is an independent statement, or we say: the meaning of 'disbelieves' is denies the rituals of Hajj and does not affirm them, and that is inconceivable with the assumed affirmation in those you mentioned.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents an objection that leaving the Hajj obligation without excuse amounts to kufr (disbelief), using Quran 3:97 which calls such a person a 'disbeliever'. The response rejects the premise, clarifying that the verse either is a separate statement not about the same person, or the term 'kufr' means denial of the Hajj obligations, not mere non-performance. Since the person in question is assumed to affirm (tasdiq) the obligation, denial is impossible, so the verse does not apply to them.

Key Terms
حج (hajj/pilgrimage)
كفر (kufr/disbelief)
تصديق (tasdiq/affirmation)
مستأنف (musta'naf/independent)
جحد (juhud/denial)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abandoning an obligatory act without excuse is kufr.
Correction: It is not kufr unless one denies the obligation itself. Mere non-performance does not amount to disbelief.

Checkpoint
How does the response interpret the word 'kufr' in Quran 3:97?
A) As mere failure to perform Hajj
B) As denial of the obligation of Hajj
C) As abandoning prayer
D) As sin without disbelief

Key Takeaway
Leaving Hajj without excuse is a major sin but not disbelief; only denying the obligation of Hajj constitutes kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refuting the Claim that Failure to Judge is Disbelief
Refutes argument that not judging by Allah's law is kufr by limiting the meaning to denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the verse 'whoever does not judge by what Allah revealed' does not necessarily condemn every failure to implement Islamic law as kufr, and how the response distinguishes between denial and mere non-implementation.

Core Idea
Not every failure to judge by Allah's law is kufr; only denial of its validity.

This lesson tackles a common misunderstanding of Quran 5:44. Some argue that any failure to judge by Allah's law constitutes disbelief. The text presents this objection and then provides a nuanced response that clarifies what the verse truly means. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first part of the passage where the opponent argues that since a person can have affirmation (tasdiq) yet fail to judge, and Allah calls such a person a disbeliever, faith must include action.
Notice the logic: tasdiq exists, but kufr is pronounced, so tasdiq alone is insufficient.
2
Identify the key verse
The objection relies on Quran 5:44. Understand the verse's literal meaning and why it is used as evidence.
The verse is often quoted out of context.
3
Understand the response's two interpretations
The response offers two possible meanings for 'does not judge by what Allah revealed': either it means 'does not affirm' (i.e., denies the law) or 'judges with something else believing it is unsuitable for judgment'. Both imply denial, not mere failure.
This shows the verse is about rejecting Allah's law, not about imperfect implementation.
4
Connect to the broader doctrine
See how this defense upholds the position that faith is affirmation (tasdiq) alone, without requiring action for its essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: التصديق موجود فيمن لم يحكم بما أنزل الله ، والله قد حكم عليه بالكفر في قوله سبحانه: ﴿وَمَن لَّمْ يَحْكُم بِمَا أَنزَلَ اللَّهُ فَأُولَيكَ هُمُ الكَفِرُونَ ﴾ [المائدة: ٤٤] ، فدل ذلك على أن الإيمان هو التصديق والعمل. ويجاب عن هذا بمثل ما أجبنا به عن الآية السابقة من الوجهين، وحاصله : أنَّ معنى: (من لم يحكم بما أنزل الله من لم يصدق ، أو من لم يحكم بشيء مما أنزل الله معتقدا أنه لا يصلح للحكم، أو نحو ذلك.
They said: Affirmation exists in one who does not judge by what Allah has revealed, and Allah has pronounced him a disbeliever in His words: 'And whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed, those are the disbelievers' [Quran 5:44]. So that indicates that faith is affirmation and action. And the response to this is similar to what we answered with the previous verse in two ways. Its summary is that the meaning of 'whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed' is whoever does not affirm, or whoever does not judge with anything of what Allah revealed believing that it is not suitable for judgment, or something similar.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents an objection that since a person may have affirmation (tasdiq) yet fail to judge by Allah's law, and Quran 5:44 calls them disbelievers, then faith must include action. The response reiterates the same two responses as before: either the verse refers to one who does not affirm (the law), or one who judges by something else believing it to be unsuitable. In either case, the person with mere failure to judge without denial is not included.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm/judgment)
كفر (kufr)
تصديق (tasdiq)
عمل (amal/action)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any failure to judge by Islamic law, even without denial, constitutes disbelief (kufr).
Correction: The verse only applies to those who deny the validity of Allah's law or believe it is unsuitable for judgment. Mere non-implementation without denial is not kufr.

Checkpoint
According to the response, what is the meaning of 'does not judge by what Allah has revealed' in Quran 5:44?
A) Anyone who makes a mistake in judgment
B) Anyone who does not judge by Islamic law
C) One who denies the validity of Allah's law
D) One who judges based on analogy

Key Takeaway
The verse refers to those who deny Allah's law, not those who fail to implement it for other reasons.

Refuting the Claim that Sins Nullify Faith
Refutes hadith that zina and drinking negate iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how theologians reinterpret the hadith about the fornicator and drinker to defend the position that major sins do not nullify faith.

Core Idea
The hadith about sin and faith refers to those who deem sins permissible, not ordinary sinners.

In this passage, the author addresses an objection based on a well-known hadith that seems to suggest that acts like fornication and drinking wine negate faith. The response offers two careful interpretations to show that the hadith does not prove that actions are part of the reality of iman. By the end, you'll see how the same hadith can support the Ash'ari view that faith is assent, not action.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and hadith
Read the passage's opening: opponents cite the hadith 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer...' as evidence that actions are part of faith.
Notice that the hadith seems clear, but context matters.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Find the two responses: first, the hadith applies only to those who consider the act permissible (mustahill); second, 'believer' here means 'safe from punishment'.
These interpretations preserve the doctrine that faith is solely assent.
3
Understand 'mustahill'
Reflect on why considering a sin permissible is actual disbelief (kufr), while committing the sin without deeming it permissible is not kufr.
This distinction is key in Islamic theology.
4
Consider the alternative meaning
Examine the second possibility: that 'mu'min' in the hadith means 'safe from punishment', not 'believer'.
This shows how careful interpretation is used to defend theological principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: الزاني وشارب الخمر ونحوهما كفار ; بدليل قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «لا يزني الزاني وهو مؤمن، ولا يشرب الخمر حين يشربها وهو مؤمن وذلك دليل على أن الإيمان يتضمن العمل. ويجاب عن ذلك بأنَّ المراد: هو الذي يزني وهو مُستحل لِزِنَاهُ، والذي يشرب الخمر مستحلا لشربها ، أو المراد بمؤمن في قوله : وهو مؤمن آمِنْ مِن عذاب الله تعالى
They said: The fornicator and the wine drinker and the like are disbelievers, as evidence of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer, nor does the wine drinker drink while he is a believer.' And that is evidence that faith includes action. And the response to that is that what is meant is the one who fornicates while considering it permissible (mustahill), and the one who drinks wine while considering it permissible, or the meaning of 'believer' in his saying 'while he is a believer' is one who is safe from Allah's punishment.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents an objection using a well-known hadith that a fornicator or drinker is not a believer at the time of the act, implying that faith includes action. The response offers two interpretations: first, the hadith refers to those who consider the act permissible (mustahill), which is actual kufr; second, that 'believer' here means one who is safe from punishment, not the actual believer. Thus the hadith does not prove that action is part of the reality of iman.

Key Terms
زنا (zina/fornication)
شرب الخمر (sharb al-khamr/wine drinking)
إيمان (iman)
مستحل (mustahill/considering permissible)
آمن (amin/safe)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any major sin like zina or drinking wine nullifies a person's faith entirely.
Correction: The response clarifies that the hadith only applies to those who consider these acts permissible (mustahill), which is disbelief, or the word 'believer' means 'safe from punishment', so it does not negate faith for ordinary sinners.

Checkpoint
According to the response, what is one interpretation of the hadith 'The fornicator does not fornicate while he is a believer'?
A) It means the person is a hypocrite
B) It applies only to those who consider fornication permissible
C) It means the person loses faith temporarily
D) It means the person must perform a kaffarah

Key Takeaway
The hadith about fornicators and drinkers is about those who consider sins permissible, not about ordinary believers who sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does the lesson's teaching about iman being unaffected by sin challenge that feeling? What would it mean for you to hold onto your identity as a believer even after falling into sin?

The lesson warns against 'mustahill'—deeming a sin permissible. Examine your own heart: Are there any sins you have rationalized, minimized, or made 'small' in your mind? What would it take for you to repent sincerely and restore the gravity of that sin before Allah?
?

How does the lesson's emphasis on the hadith being about safety from punishment, not faith, call you to take sin seriously while still trusting in Allah's mercy? Definition of Iman as Tasdiq and Its Levels
Defines iman as tasdiq and explains its conditions and levels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of iman as tasdiq, the condition of necessity for knowledge from the Prophet, and the difference between general (ijmal) and detailed (tafsil) belief.

Core Idea
Iman is affirmation of what the Prophet brought, known by necessity; general belief suffices for most matters, but detailed belief is more complete.

This passage from the Ithaaf al-Mureed commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid lays the foundation for understanding the reality of iman. It clarifies that iman is not simply belief in the heart, but a specific affirmation (tasdiq) of everything the Prophet conveyed that has become widespread in Islam. It then explains two levels of belief: general and detailed, each with its own scope.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the English translation. Notice the concise style of the matn and the explanatory nature of the sharh.
The Arabic text is incomplete at the end; the conditional clause is cut off.
2
Identify the core definition of iman
Find the statement that defines iman as tasdiq. Note that it specifies 'the legally recognized affirmation' and ties it to affirming everything the Prophet brought.
3
Understand the condition 'known by necessity'
The passage explains that matters known by necessity are those so widespread that common people know them without proof, even if they are originally theoretical. Example: oneness of God, obligation of prayer.
This condition limits what must be affirmed for valid iman.
4
Distinguish between general and detailed belief
The passage states that general (ijmal) belief suffices for matters considered generally (e.g., belief in most prophets and angels), while detailed (tafsil) belief is required for matters considered in detail (e.g., specific prophets like Adam, Muhammad, Gabriel). Detailed belief is more complete.
This distinction addresses common misunderstandings about what detailed knowledge is necessary.
5
Reflect on the incomplete conclusion
The passage ends mid-sentence: 'So if one does not affirm the obligation of...'. Consider what the conclusion likely is: that such a person would not be considered a believer.
This emphasizes the practical implication of the definition.

Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage defines iman (faith) as tasdiq (affirmation) in the legal sense. It explains that tasdiq must be of everything brought by the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) that is known from him by necessity—meaning matters that have become so widespread among Muslims that knowledge of them is akin to necessary knowledge, even if originally theoretical. Examples include the oneness of the Creator and the obligation of prayer. The passage then distinguishes between general (ijmal) belief, which suffices for matters that are known in general, like belief in most prophets and angels, and detailed (tafsil) belief, which is required for matters known in detail and is more complete, such as knowing Adam, Muhammad, and Gabriel specifically. The passage ends with the conditional that if one does not affirm the obligation of prayer when asked, they would not be considered a believer.

Misconception: Some think iman requires detailed knowledge of all matters individually, including every prophet and angel.
Correction: The passage clarifies that general belief suffices for matters known in general; detailed belief is required only for matters known in detail and is more complete but not obligatory for all.

The Reality of Faith as Affirmation
Sanusi defines iman as tasdiq in the Sharia sense and explains its conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that iman (faith) in the Sharia is defined as tasdiq (affirmation) of the Prophet in all matters known by necessity, and that this affirmation requires submission and acceptance, not mere mental acknowledgment.

Core Idea
Faith is not just knowing the truth; it is submitting to it.

This passage from Sanusi's Jawharat al-Tawhid defines the very nature of faith (iman). It distinguishes between mere mental assent and true belief that transforms one's life. The author lays out the conditions that make iman valid, emphasizing that it must be accompanied by acceptance and submission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author's own words establish the definition.
Notice the key terms: إيمان, تصديق, ضرورة, إجمال, تفصيل, تسليم.
2
Identify the definition and 'by necessity'
Find where Sanusi defines iman and how he explains 'by necessity'. What examples does he give?
3
Understand the ijmāl/tafsīl distinction
Look at the distinction between general and detailed belief. Why is detailed belief more complete?
He uses examples of prophets and angels.
4
Grasp the clarification on tasdiq
The author clarifies that tasdiq is not mere mental acknowledgment. What additional elements does he require?
This refutes a common misunderstanding.
5
Connect to taslim
Note how the passage ties iman to the concept of submission (taslim). What does the root āmana mean?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان حقيقة الإيمان (بالتَّصْدِيقِ) المعهودِ شرعاً، وهو تصديق نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم في كلِّ مَا عُلم مجيئه به مِن الدِّين بالضَّرورة، أي فيما اشتهر بين أهل الإسلام وصارَ العِلمُ به يشابه العلم الحاصل بالضّرورة، بحيث يعلمه العامة من غير افتقار إلى نظر واستدلال، وإن كان في أصله نظريًّا، كوحدة الصانع، ووجوب الصَّلاة ونحوها، ويكفي الإجمالُ فيما يُلاحظ إجمالا، كالإيمان بغالب الأنبياء والملائكة، ولا بدَّ مِن التَّفصيل فيما يُلاحَظ كذلك، وهو أكمل مِن الأوَّل، كالإيمان بجمع من الأنبياء والملائكة، كآدم ومحمد وجبريل عليهم الصلاة والسَّلام، فلو لم يُصَدِّق بوجوبِ الصلاة ونحوها عند السُّؤال عنه يكون كافراً. والمراد من تصديقه صلى الله عليه وسلم: قبول ما جاءَ به مع الرّضا بترك التكبر والعِناد؛ وبناء الأعمال عليه، لا مجرَّد وقوع نسبة الصدق إليه في القلب من غير إذعان وقبول له، حتّى يلزمَ الحُكْم بإيمان كثير من الكفَّار الذين كانوا عالمين بحقيَّة نبوته وما جاء به؛ لأنَّهم لم يكونوا أَذْعنوا لذلك ولا قَبلُوه ولا بنوا الأعمال الصَّالحة عليه، بحيثُ صارَ يُطلق عليه اسم التسليم كما هو مدلوله الوضعي؛ لأنَّ حقيقة آمن به آمَنَهُ التَّكذِيبَ والمُخالفة وجَعَلَهُ في أمن من ذلك.
An explanation of the reality of faith: by the familiar affirmation (tasdiq) according to the Sharia, and it is the affirmation of our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, in everything that is known to have come from him of the religion by necessity (bi al-darura), i.e., in that which has become widespread among the people of Islam and knowledge of it has become similar to knowledge obtained by necessity, such that the common people know it without needing reflection and inference, even if in origin it is theoretical, like the oneness of the Creator and the obligation of prayer and the like. And general (belief) suffices in matters observed generally, like belief in most prophets and angels, and detailed (belief) is necessary in matters observed in detail, and it is more complete than the first, like belief in a group of prophets and angels, such as Adam, Muhammad, and Gabriel, peace be upon them. So if one does not affirm the obligation of prayer and the like when asked about it, he becomes a disbeliever. And what is meant by affirming him, peace be upon him, is accepting what he brought with satisfaction, abandoning pride and stubbornness, and building deeds upon it, not merely the occurrence of attributing truthfulness to him in the heart without submission and acceptance, for that would entail ruling that many of the disbelievers who knew the truth of his prophethood and what he brought are believers, because they did not submit to that nor accept it nor build righteous deeds upon it, such that the name 'submission' (taslim) is applied to it as is its lexical meaning, because the reality of 'to believe in him' (āmana bihī) is to give him security from denial and opposition and to place him in safety from that.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the reality of faith (iman). It begins by defining iman as 'affirmation' (tasdiq) in the sharia sense, which is affirming the Prophet in everything known to have come from him by necessity—meaning matters that have become so widespread and well-known among Muslims that even the common person knows them without needing to reason, like the oneness of God and the obligation of prayer. The author then distinguishes between general belief (ijmāl) for general matters and detailed belief (tafsīl) for specific matters, stating that detailed belief is more complete. He provides examples: general belief suffices for most prophets and angels, while detailed belief is required for specific ones like Adam, Muhammad, and Gabriel. He then clarifies the meaning of 'affirmation' to avoid misunderstanding: it is not mere mental acknowledgment but includes acceptance with satisfaction, abandoning pride, and building actions upon it. This is supported by the fact that many disbelievers recognized the truth of the Prophet but did not submit, so they cannot be considered believers. The passage concludes by linking iman to the concept of 'submission' (taslim), emphasizing that iman places one in safety from denial and opposition.

Key Terms
إيمان
تصديق
ضرورة
إجمال
تفصيل
تسليم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mere mental acknowledgment of the Prophet's truthfulness constitutes iman.
Correction: The passage clarifies that iman requires submission, acceptance, and building deeds; otherwise many disbelievers who knew the truth would be believers.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimal condition for faith (iman) in matters known by necessity?
A) General affirmation without detail
B) Detailed affirmation for every matter
C) Affirmation with submission and acceptance
D) Mere mental acknowledgment

Key Takeaway
True faith (iman) is active submission to the Prophet's message, not passive acknowledgment.

?

?
Your deeds are part of your faith. Look at your daily actions: which ones are clearly built upon the Prophet's message, and which are merely habitual or cultural? What is one deed you will start doing solely out of submission to him?

The Two Meanings of Tasdiq in the Sharia
Explains two meanings of tasdiq and their consequences for iman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Islamic faith requires a specific type of affirmation (tasdiq) — one that includes submission (idh'ān) and certainty, not merely recognition.

Core Idea
Faith requires more than knowing the truth; it demands submission.

In discussions of iman (faith), scholars use the term tasdiq (affirmation) in two different senses. One is decisive conviction that leads to acceptance and action. The other is mere recognition of truth without any commitment. This crucial distinction determines whether someone is considered a believer. The commentator clarifies both meanings and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation to get an overview of the two meanings of tasdiq.
Notice the commentator references an earlier discussion.
2
Identify the first meaning
Locate the first meaning: 'decisive conviction' (jazm/qaṭ') also called 'submission' (idh'ān). Note that it implies acceptance and action.
3
Identify the second meaning
Find the second meaning: 'mere recognition' (ma'rifa mujarrada) without submission. Note that it existed among disbelievers.
4
Examine the proof
Look at the verse from Sura al-Baqara 2:89 that shows disbelievers recognized the truth but did not submit.
The verse is quoted as evidence.
5
Reflect on the implication
Understand why only the first meaning qualifies as iman in the Sharia.
Faith requires the internal submission that leads to action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قد عرفت مما حررناه لك في أثناء شرح المذهب الأوَّل من مذاهب العلماء في بيان حقيقة الإيمان الشرعية أنَّ التصديق يطلق على معنيين: أحدهما: الجزم والقطع بالشيء بحيث لا يكون عند صاحبه شيء من التردد والحيرة والشك، وهذا هو المعنى الذي يُعبّر العلماء عنه بالإذعان، ويقابله بهذا المعنى الإنكار، ولا شك أنَّ هذا المعنى متى وجد عند شخص كان قابلا لما صَدَّقَ به راضياً به تاركاً لكل ما يناقضه، وإلا لم يكن مُصدقًا بهذا المعنى ضرورة أنَّ العاقل يسير على وفق ما أداه إليه نظره وأذعن له فكره وسلم به عقله. والمعنى الثاني من معاني التصديق المعرفة المجردة عن الإذعان والجزم، وهذه المعرفة هي المقابلة للجهالة والنكارة، والتصديق بهذا المعنى كان موجودا عند كثير من الكفار وأهل الكتاب الذين لم يؤمنوا بما جاء به الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم، وآية ذلك قوله: {فَلَمَّا جَاءَهُم مَّا عَرَفُوا كَفَرُوا به} [البقرة: 89] فدل على أنَّ التصديق بهذا المعنى لا يستلزم إذعان المُصدِّقِ لما عرفه ولا انقياده له ولا تسليمه به ولا أن يترك ما يناقضه.
You have known from what we have written for you in the explanation of the first opinion among the opinions of the scholars in the statement of the reality of faith according to the Sharia that affirming (tasdiq) is used in two meanings: One of them: decisive conviction and certainty of a thing such that there is no trace of hesitation, perplexity, or doubt with its possessor. This is the meaning that scholars express as 'submission' (idh'ān), and its opposite in this meaning is 'denial' (inkār). There is no doubt that when this meaning is found in a person, he is accepting of what he affirmed, satisfied with it, leaving everything that contradicts it; otherwise he would not be an affirmer in this meaning, necessarily, because a rational person acts in accordance with what his reflection has led him to, and his intellect has submitted to, and his mind has accepted. The second meaning of the meanings of affirming is mere recognition (ma'rifa) stripped of submission and conviction. This recognition is the opposite of ignorance and unfamiliarity (nakāra). Affirmation in this meaning existed among many of the disbelievers and People of the Book who did not believe in what the Messenger brought. The proof of that is His statement: 'But when there came to them that which they recognized, they disbelieved in it' [al-Baqara 2:89]. This indicates that affirmation in this meaning does not entail the affirmer's submission to what he recognized, nor his compliance with it, nor his acceptance of it, nor that he leave what contradicts it.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory note that clarifies the two distinct meanings of 'affirmation' (tasdiq) as used in discussions of faith. It begins by reminding the reader of an earlier discussion. The first meaning is decisive conviction (jazm) and certainty (qaṭ') with no doubt, which scholars call 'submission' (idh'ān). This meaning necessarily implies that the person accepts and acts upon what he affirms, because a rational person behaves consistently with his conviction. The second meaning is mere recognition (ma'rifa) without conviction or submission. This meaning was present among the disbelievers and People of the Book who recognized the truth of the Prophet but rejected it. The commentator cites the verse from Sura al-Baqara to prove that such recognition does not entail faith. Thus, faith requires the first meaning of tasdiq, not the second.

Key Terms
تصديق
إذعان
جزم
معرفة
إنكار
نكارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that simply knowing the truth of Islam (e.g., acknowledging the Prophet's truthfulness) is sufficient for faith.
Correction: True iman requires the first meaning of tasdiq: decisive conviction that leads to inner submission (idh'ān) and outward compliance.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes the first meaning of tasdiq from the second?
A) The first meaning is only for scholars, the second for common people
B) The first meaning includes submission (idh'ān) and certainty, while the second is mere recognition
C) The first meaning is about the Prophet, the second about the Quran
D) The first meaning is stronger in terms of knowledge

Key Takeaway
True faith (iman) requires the first type of tasdiq: a decisive conviction that leads to inner submission and outward compliance, not just intellectual recognition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Think of an area in your life where you know you should change but haven't. Which meaning of tasdiq is missing there?
?
The disbelievers in the verse recognized the truth but rejected it. Is there any truth you recognize but resist? Why?

The Obligation to Utter the Two Testimonies: Condition or Part?
Sanusi states the requirement to utter the shahadatayn and points to the dispute over its role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to utter the two testimonies and the scholarly dispute over whether utterance is a condition or part of faith.

Core Idea
Uttering the shahadatayn is required, but scholars differ on its role in faith.

The passage begins by stating the basic requirement: a capable Muslim must utter the two testimonies. But immediately, Sanusi points to a deeper dispute: is this utterance a condition for faith or a part of it? The footnote clarifies that both sides agree utterance has involvement; the debate is over the nature of that involvement. This lesson unpacks that foundational question.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's main statement.
Pay attention to the footnote indicators (1) and (2).
2
Identify the dispute
The passage references a dispute about 'the aspect of involvement.' Find where the footnote explains the two positions: condition (shart) vs. part (shitr).
Note that the scholars agree on involvement but differ on its nature.
3
Reflect on implications
Consider why this distinction matters: if utterance is a condition, it is external to faith; if it is a part, it is internal. How might this affect rulings on who is considered a believer?
This connects to broader issues in theology and law.
